Session has the SKU with force verification\nAcceptance Criteria\nFor all scenarios below, unless otherwise specified:\nVIP user = a customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list configured in Split (sourced from CS’ VIP list – personal accounts only).\n\nNon‑VIP user = a customer whose Customer ID is not present in that VIP list.\n\nS&G checkout = Scan & Go purchase flow in physical stores.\n\nRestricted / high‑risk products = products that would normally trigger S&G verification per current rules (e.g., high-priced items, high fraud risk, suspicious patterns, etc.). VIPs MUST still be verified for high-priced items.\n\nAge‑restricted items = items tagged as requiring age verification.\n\nForce‑verification SKUs = SKUs that are explicitly configured to always require verification, regardless of other rules.\n\nVIP bypass logic = new logic where VIPs skip S&G verification for all rules except:\nAge‑restricted items\n\nForce‑verification SKUs\n\nHigh-priced items (items with price > HighRiskPrice threshold)\n\n\n\n\n1. Common Scenarios (VIP bypass works as intended)\n1.1 VIP user with only non‑restricted items – no verification\nScenario 1.1 – VIP bypass with non‑restricted basket\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout in a participating store\nAND the basket contains only non‑restricted, non‑high‑risk items\nAND no age‑restricted items are present\nAND no SKUs in the basket are marked as force‑verification\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout and reaches the normal verification decision step\n\nThen the system MUST bypass the S&G verification step\nAND the customer MUST be allowed to complete payment without any S&G verification prompt\nAND the order status MUST be the same as for a successfully verified order.\n\n\n1.2 VIP user with items that would normally trigger generic risk rules – still bypassed\nScenario 1.2 – VIP bypass for generic risk‑based rules\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND the basket contains products or patterns that would normally trigger non‑age, non‑forced, non-high-priced S&G verification rules (e.g., abnormal basket value, frequency‑based risk rule, etc.)\nAND no age‑restricted items are present\nAND no SKUs in the basket are marked as force‑verification\nAND no high-priced items are present\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout and the verification rules are evaluated\n\nThen the system MUST ignore / bypass those generic S&G verification rules for this transaction\nAND the customer MUST NOT be prompted for S&G verification\nAND the order MUST proceed directly to completion without verification.\n\n\n1.3 VIP user with age‑restricted items but no force‑verification SKUs – only age verification applied\nScenario 1.3 – VIP still subject to age‑restricted rule\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND the basket contains at least one age‑restricted item\nAND the basket contains no SKUs marked as force‑verification\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout and the verification rules are evaluated\n\nThen the system MUST still apply the age‑restriction verification rule as per current logic\nAND the customer MUST be prompted for appropriate age verification\nAND all other non‑age, non‑forced verification rules MUST be bypassed for this VIP user.\n\n\n1.4 VIP user with force‑verification SKU but no age‑restricted items – force verification applied\nScenario 1.4 – VIP still subject to force‑verification SKUs\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND the basket contains at least one SKU that is configured as force‑verification\nAND the basket contains no age‑restricted items\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout and the verification rules are evaluated\n\nThen the system MUST still trigger S&G verification due to the force‑verification SKU\nAND the customer MUST be prompted for S&G verification as per the existing force‑verification flow\nAND all other non‑age, non‑forced verification rules MUST be bypassed for this VIP user.\n\n\n1.5 VIP user with both age‑restricted and force‑verification items – verification still required\nScenario 1.5 – VIP with both age‑restricted and force‑verification SKUs\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND the basket contains at least one age‑restricted item\nAND the basket contains at least one SKU configured as force‑verification\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout and the verification rules are evaluated\n\nThen the system MUST trigger S&G verification (driven by the age‑restricted rule and/or force‑verification SKU)\nAND the customer MUST be prompted for S&G verification as per the strictest applicable existing flow\nAND all other non‑age, non‑forced verification rules MUST be bypassed.\n\n\n1.6 Non‑VIP users – behaviour unchanged\nScenario 1.6 – Non‑VIP user retains existing verification logic\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is not present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND any combination of products is in the basket\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout and the verification rules are evaluated\n\nThen the S&G verification behaviour MUST remain identical to the pre‑VIP‑bypass implementation\nAND the presence or configuration of the VIP Split flag MUST NOT change the verification decision for this user.\n\n\n2. Edge Cases and Boundary Conditions\n2.1 VIP Split flag disabled – VIP bypass not applied\nScenario 2.1 – Feature flag disabled\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is disabled or not rolled out to this customer/environment\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND any combination of products is in the basket\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout\n\nThen the system MUST apply the original S&G verification rules as if the VIP bypass feature does not exist\nAND the customer MUST be treated as a non‑VIP for verification decisions.\n\n\n2.2 VIP list empty in Split – all users treated as non‑VIP\nScenario 2.2 – Empty VIP list configuration\nGiven the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the VIP customer ID list configured in Split is empty (no Customer IDs)\n\nWhen any customer (of any type) proceeds to S&G checkout\n\nThen no customer MUST be treated as VIP for verification purposes\nAND all S&G verification decisions MUST follow the existing non‑VIP logic.\n\n\n2.3 Customer ID not resolvable – fallback to non‑VIP behaviour\nScenario 2.3 – Missing or unresolvable Customer ID\nGiven a customer is using S&G checkout\nAND due to a data or integration issue the system cannot reliably resolve the customer’s Customer ID\nOR the Customer ID is not present in the request context where VIP evaluation is performed\n\nWhen the system evaluates whether the user is VIP\n\nThen the system MUST default to treating the user as non‑VIP\nAND apply existing S&G verification rules with no VIP bypass.\n\n\n2.4 VIP list lookup failure (Split outage / timeout) – safe fallback\nScenario 2.4 – Split unresponsive or returns error\nGiven a customer is using S&G checkout\nAND the system attempts to evaluate VIP status using Split\nAND the Split call to retrieve the VIP list or evaluate the flag fails (e.g., timeout, network error, 5xx, malformed response)\n\nWhen the VIP evaluation cannot be reliably completed\n\nThen the system MUST safely default to treating the user as non‑VIP\nAND apply existing S&G verification logic without any VIP bypass\nAND the failure MUST be logged with sufficient details for operational monitoring (without impacting customer‑facing flow beyond standard verification).\n\n\n2.5 VIP user with combination of restricted and non‑restricted items – rule precedence\nScenario 2.5 – Mixed basket precedence for VIP\nGiven a logged‑in customer whose Customer ID is present in the VIP list in Split\nAND the VIP Split flag is enabled\nAND the customer is using S&G checkout\nAND the basket contains both:\nnon‑restricted, non‑high‑risk items, and\n\none or more items that are either age‑restricted or force‑verification SKUs\n\n\n\nWhen the customer proceeds to S&G checkout\n\nThen the presence of any age‑restricted or force‑verification SKU MUST take precedence\nAND the system MUST trigger S&G verification according to the strongest applicable rule\nAND VIP bypass MUST only apply to the remaining non‑age, non‑forced rules.\n\n\n2.6 Non‑personal accounts excluded from VIP list\nScenario 2.6 – Only personal accounts treated as VIP\nGiven the VIP list configured in Split is derived from CS’ list of VIP customers\nAND it only includes personal customer accounts (as per technical notes)\nAND a logged‑in customer is using a non‑personal account type (e.g., corporate / business) during S&G checkout\n\nWhen the system evaluates VIP status\n\nThen this customer MUST NOT be considered VIP based solely on a non‑personal account\nAND existing S&G verification rules MUST apply with no VIP bypass.\n\n\n2.7 Multiple environments / test users – controlled via Split\nScenario 2.7 – Environment and rollout control\nGiven the VIP bypass feature is controlled via Split\nAND specific environments or cohorts are configured in Split to include or exclude certain users as VIP\n\nWhen a customer proceeds to S&G checkout in any environment\n\nThen their VIP status MUST be determined solely based on:\nmembership of their Customer ID in the VIP list configured for that environment/cohort in Split, and\n\nthe flag state for
